high\nallowed-tools: Read, Glob, Grep, Edit, Write, Bash, TodoWrite, Task\nmcp-servers: [sequential, serena, context7, auggie-mcp]\npersonas: [architect, analyzer, backend]\nargument-hint: \"--workflow <skill-name-or-path> [--name <cli-name>] [--output <dir>] [--dry-run] [--skip-integration]\"\n---\n\n# sc:cli-portify — Workflow-to-CLI Pipeline Compiler\n\nConvert inference-based SuperClaude workflows into programmatic CLI pipelines that ensure 100% completion and consistency between runs.\n\n## Purpose\n\nSuperClaude workflows implemented as commands + skills + agents + refs rely entirely on Claude's reasoning for orchestration. This works well for flexible, one-off tasks but breaks down for repeatable multi-step pipelines where you need:\n\n- **Deterministic control flow** — Python decides what runs when, not inference\n- **Formal artifact validation** — Gates check output quality programmatically\n- **Resume/retry** — Failed steps resume without re-running everything\n- **Live monitoring** — TUI shows progress, stall detection, diagnostics\n- **Budget economics** — Turn ledger tracks consumption across subprocesses\n- **Consistent behavior** — Same inputs produce structurally identical outputs every run\n\nThe existing `pipeline/` and `sprint/` modules already solve these problems. This skill bridges the gap by analyzing a workflow and generating a new CLI module that uses these proven patterns.\n\n## What Gets Generated\n\nA CLI subcommand package under `src/superclaude/cli/<name>/`:\n\n| File | Purpose | When Generated |\n|------|---------|----------------|\n| `models.py` | Domain types extending `PipelineConfig`, `Step`, `StepResult` | Always |\n| `gates.py` | `GateCriteria` + semantic check functions returning `tuple[bool, str]` | Always |\n| `prompts.py` | LLM contract builders per Claude-assisted step | Always |\n| `config.py` | CLI arg resolution, file discovery, config construction | Always |\n| `executor.py` | Synchronous supervisor loop with `ThreadPoolExecutor` for parallelism | Always |\n| `monitor.py` | NDJSON incremental output parser with domain signals | Always |\n| `process.py` | `ClaudeProcess` subclass with domain-specific prompt building | Always |\n| `tui.py` | Rich live dashboard with gate state machine | Always |\n| `logging_.py` | Dual JSONL + Markdown execution logging | Always |\n| `diagnostics.py` | `DiagnosticCollector`, `FailureClassifier`, `ReportGenerator` | Always |\n| `commands.py` | Click CLI group and subcommands | Always |\n| `__init__.py` | Package exports | Always |\n| `inventory.py` | Pure-programmatic file discovery/classification | If workflow has discovery steps |\n| `filtering.py` | Pure-programmatic inter-step data filtering | If workflow has filtering between steps |\n\nThese file definitions inform the pipeline specification produced in Phase 2.\n\n## Required Input\n\n```\n/sc:cli-portify --workflow <skill-name-or-path> [--name <cli-name>] [--output <dir>]\n```\n\n| Argument | Required | Description |\n|----------|----------|-------------|\n| `--workflow` | Yes | Skill directory path or `sc-*` name to portify |\n| `--name` | No | CLI subcommand name (default: derived from workflow) |\n| `--output` | No | Output directory (default: `src/superclaude/cli/<name>/`) |\n| `--dry-run` | No | Show decomposition plan without generating spec |\n\n**STOP** if `--workflow` is not provided or the path doesn't resolve to a valid skill.\n\n## Behavioral Flow\n\nFour phases, each producing artifacts that feed the next. Present output to user for review after Phases 1 and 2 before continuing.\n\n### Phase 1: Workflow Analysis\n\nLoad `refs/analysis-protocol.md` before this phase. It contains the discovery checklist, step decomposition algorithm, classification rubric, and output format template.\n\n**Goal**: Decompose the target workflow into a structured pipeline specification.\n\n1. **Discover components** — Find the command `.md`, skill `SKILL.md`, all `refs/` and `rules/`, all `templates/`, all `scripts/`, and all referenced agents. Build a component inventory table with paths, line counts, and purposes.\n\n2. **Map the protocol** — Extract the step-by-step behavioral flow. Pay attention to:\n   - Wave/phase boundaries in the skill\n   - Agent delegation patterns (which agent, parallel vs sequential)\n   - Conditional execution paths (flags that skip steps)\n   - Implicit inter-step data flow (what one step produces that another consumes)\n\n3. **Identify steps** — A new Step boundary exists when:\n   - A new artifact is produced\n   - A different agent takes over\n   - Execution mode changes (sequential → parallel)\n   - A quality gate must be evaluated\n   - Operation type changes (analysis → generation → validation)\n\n4. **Classify each step** on the programmatic spectrum:\n   - **Pure programmatic**: Runs as a Python function, no Claude subprocess. Examples: file inventory via `git ls-files`, config construction, file filtering between passes, scoring formulas, structural validation, batch assignment. If the logic is deterministic and the input/output formats are well-defined, it should be programmatic.\n   - **Claude-assisted**: Runs as a Claude subprocess with a prompt contract and gate. Examples: content analysis, writing reports, rubric-based assessment, creative synthesis, debate.\n   - **Hybrid**: Programmatic setup → Claude subprocess → programmatic validation. Examples: steps that need Claude for content but have strict structural validation on the output.\n\n5. **Map dependencies and parallel groups** — Draw the data flow: which steps produce artifacts consumed by downstream steps? Which steps are independent and can run concurrently? For batched workflows, identify where batch parallelism applies.\n\n6. **Extract gates** — For each step output, identify what validation the original workflow expects. Map these to gate tiers: EXEMPT (informational), LIGHT (exists + non-empty), STANDARD (structural checks), STRICT (structural + semantic).\n\n7. **Assign gate modes** — `GateMode.BLOCKING` for steps whose output feeds downstream steps. `GateMode.TRAILING` for quality-only checks that don't affect data flow.\n\n**Output**: `portify-analysis.md` — Complete decomposition following the template in `refs/analysis-protocol.md`. Must include: component inventory, step graph with classifications, parallel groups, gates summary, data flow diagram, and recommendations.\n\n**Present to user for review before Phase 2.**\n\n### Phase 2: Pipeline Specification\n\nLoad `refs/pipeline-spec.md` before this phase. It contains Step definition patterns, model design patterns, gate patterns, executor patterns, and the new unified-audit-gating patterns (TurnLedger, gate modes, subprocess isolation, context injection, resume semantics).\n\n**Goal**: Convert the analysis into concrete, code-ready specifications.\n\n1. **Design the Step graph** — Map each workflow step to `Step` objects. Batched parallel steps are `list[Step]` groups. Dynamic step counts (e.g., batch count determined at runtime) require a `build_steps()` function.\n\n2. **Define models** — Design domain-specific dataclasses:\n   - Config extending `PipelineConfig` with workflow-specific fields (source paths, pass selection, batch sizes, stall/timeout policies)\n   - Status enum with domain-specific states (e.g., `VALIDATION_FAIL`, `CRITICAL_FAIL` for audit workflows)\n   - Result extending `StepResult` with execution telemetry\n   - Aggregate result with `resume_command()` and `suggested_resume_budget`\n   - Monitor state with domain-specific NDJSON signals\n   - `TurnLedger` integration for budget tracking\n\n3. **Design prompts** — For each Claude-assisted step, write the prompt builder. Each prompt must specify:\n   - What input files/context to embed (inline for <50KB, `--file` args for larger)\n   - Required output sections and frontmatter fields\n   - Machine-readable markers: `EXIT_RECOMMENDATION: CONTINUE|HALT`\n   - Any structural requirements the gate will check\n\n   If prompts collectively exceed ~300 lines, put them in a separate `portify-prompts.md`.\n\n4. **Design gates** — For each output artifact, define:\n   - `GateCriteria` with tier, required frontmatter, min lines, semantic checks\n   - `GateMode` (BLOCKING or TRAILING)\n   - All semantic check functions returning `tuple[bool, str]`\n\n5. **Implement pure-programmatic steps** — Write actual runnable Python code for steps classified as \"pure programmatic\". These run as direct function calls in the executor, bypassing `ClaudeProcess`. Include: file discovery, domain classification, batch assignment, inter-pass filtering, config construction.\n\n6. **Design the executor** — Sprint-style synchronous supervisor:\n   - `ThreadPoolExecutor` for batch parallelism (NOT async/await)\n   - `time.sleep()` polling loops for monitoring\n   - Per-step/batch monitoring with stall detection\n   - `TurnLedger` budget guards before each launch\n   - Runner-authored truth: reports from observed data, not Claude self-reporting\n   - Subprocess isolation (4-layer model) for child Claude sessions\n   - Context injection: prior results compressed into subsequent prompts\n   - Signal-aware shutdown with `SignalHandler`\n\n7. **Plan integration** — Click command group, main.py import, file generation order.\n\n**Output**: `portify-spec.md` (+ optional `portify-prompts.md`) — Complete code spec with models, gates, executor design, pure-programmatic implementations, and integration plan.\n\n**Present to user for approval before Phase 3.**\n\n### Phase 3: Release Spec Synthesis\n\n**Phase 2→3 Entry Gate**: Before beginning Phase 3, verify ALL of the following:\n- Phase 2 contract `status: completed`\n- All blocking checks passed (no unresolved BLOCKING gate failures)\n- Phase 2 `step_mapping` contains ≥1 entry\n\n**STOP** if any entry gate condition fails. Report which condition failed and emit the return contract with `failure_phase: 3, failure_type: prerequisite_failed`.\n\n**Goal**: Generate a complete, reviewed release specification from Phase 1 and Phase 2 outputs. Record the wall clock start time for `phase_3_seconds` timing instrumentation.\n\n**Timing**: Record `phase_3_start = current_time()` at the beginning of this phase. NFR-001 advisory target: Phase 3 should complete within 10 minutes wall clock (non-blocking; exceeding this target emits a warning but does not halt the pipeline).\n\n#### Step 3a: Template Instantiation\n\n1. Load the release spec template from `src/superclaude/examples/release-spec-template.md`\n2. Create a working copy at `{work_dir}/portify-release-spec.md`\n3. Verify the working copy was created successfully and contains the template content\n\n#### Step 3b: Content Population\n\nFill template sections from Phase 1 (workflow analysis) and Phase 2 (pipeline specification) outputs using the following mapping table. For each template section, replace `{{SC_PLACEHOLDER:*}}` sentinels with content derived from the specified source:\n\n| # | Template Section | Source |\n|---|-----------------|--------|\n| 1 | Problem Statement | Derive from source workflow's purpose + why portification is needed |\n| 2 | Solution Overview | Phase 2 pipeline architecture (step graph, executor design) |\n| 2.2 | Workflow / Data Flow | Phase 1 data flow diagram, adapted for the target pipeline |\n| 3 | Functional Requirements | One FR per generated pipeline step from Phase 2 `step_mapping` — every `step_mapping` entry MUST produce a corresponding FR (SC-004) |\n| 4 | Architecture | Phase 2 `module_plan` (new files), Phase 0 prerequisites (modified files) |\n| 4.5 | Data Models | Phase 2 model designs (Config, Status, Result, MonitorState) |\n| 4.6 | Implementation Order | Phase 2 module dependency order |\n| 5.2 | Gate Criteria | Phase 2 `gate_definitions` |\n| 5.3 | Phase Contracts | Phase 1+2 contract schemas |\n| 6 | NFRs | Standard portification NFRs (sync execution, gate signatures, runner-authored truth) |\n| 7 | Risk Assessment | Derived from Phase 1 classification confidence scores + unsupported patterns |\n| 8 | Test Plan | Structural test plan from Phase 2 pattern coverage matrix |\n| 10 | Downstream Inputs | Themes for sc:roadmap, tasks for sc:tasklist |\n\nAfter populating all sections, run SC-003 self-validation: verify zero remaining `{{SC_PLACEHOLDER:*}}` sentinels in the working copy. If any remain, resolve them before proceeding.\n\n#### Step 3c: Automated Brainstorm Pass\n\nApply embedded brainstorm behavioral patterns as a non-interactive automated pass against the draft spec. This is NOT an invocation of the `sc:brainstorm` command (which is interactive/Socratic); instead, cycle through each of three personas to analyze the draft spec for gaps:\n\n**Persona perspectives** (apply each in sequence):\n\n1. **Architect persona**: Analyze for structural gaps — missing dependencies, incomplete module boundaries, scaling concerns, cross-module interaction gaps, missing error handling paths\n2. **Analyzer persona**: Analyze for logical gaps — uncovered edge cases, ambiguous requirements, missing acceptance criteria, inconsistent cross-references, untestable requirements\n3. **Backend persona**: Analyze for implementation gaps — missing data models, incomplete API contracts, undefined error states, missing retry/timeout specifications, resource lifecycle gaps\n\n**Structured output format**: Each finding uses the schema:\n```\n{gap_id, description, severity(high|medium|low), affected_section, persona}\n```\n\nExample:\n```\n{GAP-001, \"No retry policy defined for failed gate checks\", medium, \"5.2 Gate Criteria\", architect}\n```\n\n**Zero-gap handling**: If no gaps are identified across all three personas, produce an explicit summary:\n> \"No gaps identified by architect, analyzer, and backend personas. Spec coverage assessed as complete.\"\n\nSet `gaps_identified: 0` in the return contract. Zero gaps is a valid outcome — it does not block the pipeline.\n\n**Output**: Append a `## Brainstorm Gap Analysis` section (Section 12) to the draft spec containing all findings in the structured format, or the zero-gap summary.\n\n#### Step 3d: Gap Incorporation\n\nReview each brainstorm finding and route it:\n\n- **Actionable findings** (findings that can be directly addressed): Incorporate into the relevant spec body section identified by `affected_section`. Mark the finding as `[INCORPORATED]` in the gap analysis table.\n- **Unresolvable items** (findings that require external input, are out of scope, or cannot be resolved within the spec): Route to Section 11 (Open Items) with the gap ID, question, impact, and resolution target. Mark the finding as `[OPEN]` in the gap analysis table.\n\nAfter incorporation, update the gap analysis summary with counts: `{total_gaps, incorporated, open, severity_distribution}`.\n\n**Timing**: Record `phase_3_end = current_time()`. Compute `phase_3_seconds = phase_3_end - phase_3_start`. Populate `phase_timing.phase_3_seconds` in the return contract. If `phase_3_seconds > 600`, emit warning: \"Phase 3 exceeded 10-minute advisory target (NFR-001)\".\n\n**Output**: `{work_dir}/portify-release-spec.md` — Complete draft spec with brainstorm gap analysis section and incorporated findings.\n\n**Phase 3→4 automatic gate**: Draft spec populated (no `{{SC_PLACEHOLDER:*}}` values remain) AND brainstorm section (Section 12) present in draft spec.\n\n### Phase 4: Spec Panel Review\n\nEmbed `sc:spec-panel` behavioral patterns in a convergent review loop. Like Phase 3's brainstorm, this embeds spec-panel behavioral patterns directly rather than invoking the `sc:spec-panel` command.\n\n**4a. Focus pass**: Apply spec-panel behavioral patterns with `--focus correctness,architecture` against `portify-release-spec.md`. This pass applies Fowler (architecture), Nygard (reliability/failure modes), Whittaker (adversarial), Crispin (testing) expert analysis. Produces guard condition boundary tables, validates pipeline dimensional analysis, and produces state variable registry if applicable.\n\n**4b. Focus incorporation**: Review focus findings. Incorporation MUST be additive-only — extend or append to spec sections, do not rewrite existing content.\n- CRITICAL findings: MUST be addressed — either incorporated into spec or documented with a written justification for dismissal in the panel report\n- MAJOR findings: incorporated into spec body\n- MINOR findings: go to Open Items if not immediately actionable\n\n**4c. Critique pass**: Apply spec-panel behavioral patterns with `--mode critique` against the updated spec. Runs the full expert panel in review sequence.\n\n**4d. Convergence check**: Compare critique findings with focus findings. If ≤3 new CRITICAL or MAJOR findings, the spec has converged. Otherwise, loop back to 4b (max 3 iterations; escalate to user if exceeded).\n\n**Present final spec to user for approval before delivering.**\n\n## Decision Framework: What Becomes Programmatic\n\nThe value of portification is moving orchestration out of inference. Here are concrete examples from tested workflows:\n\n| Operation | Classification | Why |\n|-----------|---------------|-----|\n| Enumerate repo files | Pure programmatic | `git ls-files` + pattern matching is deterministic |\n| Classify file domains | Pure programmatic | Extension/path pattern rules, no judgment needed |\n| Assign files to batches | Pure programmatic | Math: divide files by batch_size, assign to agents |\n| Filter Pass 1 results for Pass 2 | Pure programmatic | Parse markdown, extract classifications, filter list |\n| Analyze file for issues | Claude-assisted | Requires reading code, understanding context |\n| Score variant quality | Hybrid | Formulas are programmatic, rubric evaluation is Claude |\n| Validate structural integrity | Pure programmatic | Regex checks, section presence, field counts |\n| Spot-check verification | Claude-assisted | Re-reads files, re-evaluates claims independently |\n| Merge batch reports | Claude-assisted | Requires synthesis, deduplication, pattern extraction |\n| Compute convergence score | Pure programmatic | `agreed / total` — arithmetic |\n| Generate executive summary | Claude-assisted | Requires narrative synthesis |\n\n### Rule of Thumb\nIf you can write a Python function for it with clear input→output types and no ambiguity, make it programmatic. If it requires reading natural language, making judgments, or synthesizing information, use Claude with a gate to verify the output.\n\n## Pipeline Design Principles\n\nThese inform Phase 2 pipeline specification and align with the unified-audit-gating architecture in `pipeline/`.\n\n### Critical Constraints\n1. **Synchronous execution** — Sprint uses `threading` + `time.sleep()` polling. Use `concurrent.futures.ThreadPoolExecutor` for batch parallelism. Do NOT use async/await.\n2. **Gate function signatures** — All semantic checks return `tuple[bool, str]`. The reason string feeds diagnostics and retry decisions.\n3. **Runner-authored truth** — Reports derive from runner-observed data (exit codes, artifacts, gates, monitor signals), not Claude's self-reported status.\n4. **Deterministic flow control** — Python makes all decisions about what runs next. Claude never decides \"what's next\".\n\n### Shared Pipeline Patterns\n5. **Reuse `pipeline/` primitives** — `PipelineConfig`, `Step`, `StepResult`, `GateMode`, `GateCriteria`, `SemanticCheck`, `gate_passed()`, `ClaudeProcess`\n6. **Gate modes** — `BLOCKING` (default) stops pipeline on failure. `TRAILING` defers evaluation. Use trailing only for quality checks that don't affect downstream data flow.\n7. **Turn budget** — `TurnLedger` with debit/credit/guard for multi-subprocess pipelines. Pre-launch guards prevent launching when budget too low.\n8. **Subprocess isolation** — 4-layer model: scoped work dir, git ceiling, isolated plugin dir, isolated settings dir.\n9. **Context injection** — Prior results serialized into subsequent prompts. Compress older, preserve recent.\n10. **Resume-first failures** — On halt: exact resume command, remaining work, diagnostic path, budget suggestion.\n11. **Diagnostic chain** — Runner-side failure analysis that doesn't consume turn budget.\n\n### Output Guidance\n- `portify-analysis.md`: Under 400 lines. Step graph, gates, data flow.\n- `portify-spec.md`: Split prompts to separate file if spec exceeds 800 lines.\n- Pure-programmatic steps: Full implementation code, not descriptions.\n\n## Boundaries\n\n### Will Do\n- Analyze any SuperClaude skill/command/agent workflow\n- Decompose into structured pipeline specification\n- Generate complete CLI subcommand module\n- Wire module into CLI infrastructure\n- Generate structural tests for pipeline\n\n### Will Not Do\n- Execute the generated pipeline\n- Modify original skill/command/agent files\n- Create new skills or agents\n- Make architectural decisions about the workflow's logic\n- Generate LLM content quality tests (only structural)\n\n## Related Commands\n\n- `/sc:implement` — General feature implementation\n- `/sc:design` — System architecture design\n- `/sc:analyze` — Code analysis for understanding workflows\n- `/sc:build` — Build and compile after generating\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":301,"oldLines":16,"newStart":301,"newLines":16,"lines":[" ### Will Do"," - Analyze any SuperClaude skill/command/agent workflow"," - Decompose into structured pipeline specification","-- Generate complete CLI subcommand module","-- Wire module into CLI infrastructure","-- Generate structural tests for pipeline","+- Generate a complete release specification via template instantiation and brainstorm pass","+- Run spec panel review for quality validation","+- Produce a downstream-ready spec for sc:roadmap and sc:tasklist"," "," ### Will Not Do","+- Generate code files directly (use the release spec with sc:implement instead)"," - Execute the generated pipeline"," - Modify original skill/command/agent files"," - Create new skills or agents"," - Make architectural decisions about the workflow's logic","-- Generate LLM content quality tests (only structural)"," "," ## Related Commands"," "]}],"userModified":false,"replaceAll":false}}

`filtering.py` | Pure-programmatic inter-step data filtering | If workflow has filtering between steps |\n\nThese file definitions inform the pipeline specification produced in Phase 2.\n\n## Required Input\n\n```\n/sc:cli-portify --workflow <skill-name-or-path> [--name <cli-name>] [--output <dir>]\n```\n\n| Argument | Required | Description |\n|----------|----------|-------------|\n| `--workflow` | Yes | Skill directory path or `sc-*` name to portify |\n| `--name` | No | CLI subcommand name (default: derived from workflow) |\n| `--output` | No | Output directory (default: `src/superclaude/cli/<name>/`) |\n| `--dry-run` | No | Show decomposition plan without generating spec |\n\n**STOP** if `--workflow` is not provided or the path doesn't resolve to a valid skill.\n\n## Behavioral Flow\n\nFour phases, each producing artifacts that feed the next. Present output to user for review after Phases 1 and 2 before continuing.\n\n### Phase 1: Workflow Analysis\n\nLoad `refs/analysis-protocol.md` before this phase. It contains the discovery checklist, step decomposition algorithm, classification rubric, and output format template.\n\n**Goal**: Decompose the target workflow into a structured pipeline specification.\n\n1. **Discover components** — Find the command `.md`, skill `SKILL.md`, all `refs/` and `rules/`, all `templates/`, all `scripts/`, and all referenced agents. Build a component inventory table with paths, line counts, and purposes.\n\n2. **Map the protocol** — Extract the step-by-step behavioral flow. Pay attention to:\n   - Wave/phase boundaries in the skill\n   - Agent delegation patterns (which agent, parallel vs sequential)\n   - Conditional execution paths (flags that skip steps)\n   - Implicit inter-step data flow (what one step produces that another consumes)\n\n3. **Identify steps** — A new Step boundary exists when:\n   - A new artifact is produced\n   - A different agent takes over\n   - Execution mode changes (sequential → parallel)\n   - A quality gate must be evaluated\n   - Operation type changes (analysis → generation → validation)\n\n4. **Classify each step** on the programmatic spectrum:\n   - **Pure programmatic**: Runs as a Python function, no Claude subprocess. Examples: file inventory via `git ls-files`, config construction, file filtering between passes, scoring formulas, structural validation, batch assignment. If the logic is deterministic and the input/output formats are well-defined, it should be programmatic.\n   - **Claude-assisted**: Runs as a Claude subprocess with a prompt contract and gate. Examples: content analysis, writing reports, rubric-based assessment, creative synthesis, debate.\n   - **Hybrid**: Programmatic setup → Claude subprocess → programmatic validation. Examples: steps that need Claude for content but have strict structural validation on the output.\n\n5. **Map dependencies and parallel groups** — Draw the data flow: which steps produce artifacts consumed by downstream steps? Which steps are independent and can run concurrently? For batched workflows, identify where batch parallelism applies.\n\n6. **Extract gates** — For each step output, identify what validation the original workflow expects. Map these to gate tiers: EXEMPT (informational), LIGHT (exists + non-empty), STANDARD (structural checks), STRICT (structural + semantic).\n\n7. **Assign gate modes** — `GateMode.BLOCKING` for steps whose output feeds downstream steps. `GateMode.TRAILING` for quality-only checks that don't affect data flow.\n\n**Output**: `portify-analysis.md` — Complete decomposition following the template in `refs/analysis-protocol.md`. Must include: component inventory, step graph with classifications, parallel groups, gates summary, data flow diagram, and recommendations.\n\n**Present to user for review before Phase 2.**\n\n### Phase 2: Pipeline Specification\n\nLoad `refs/pipeline-spec.md` before this phase. It contains Step definition patterns, model design patterns, gate patterns, executor patterns, and the new unified-audit-gating patterns (TurnLedger, gate modes, subprocess isolation, context injection, resume semantics).\n\n**Goal**: Convert the analysis into concrete, code-ready specifications.\n\n1. **Design the Step graph** — Map each workflow step to `Step` objects. Batched parallel steps are `list[Step]` groups. Dynamic step counts (e.g., batch count determined at runtime) require a `build_steps()` function.\n\n2. **Define models** — Design domain-specific dataclasses:\n   - Config extending `PipelineConfig` with workflow-specific fields (source paths, pass selection, batch sizes, stall/timeout policies)\n   - Status enum with domain-specific states (e.g., `VALIDATION_FAIL`, `CRITICAL_FAIL` for audit workflows)\n   - Result extending `StepResult` with execution telemetry\n   - Aggregate result with `resume_command()` and `suggested_resume_budget`\n   - Monitor state with domain-specific NDJSON signals\n   - `TurnLedger` integration for budget tracking\n\n3. **Design prompts** — For each Claude-assisted step, write the prompt builder. Each prompt must specify:\n   - What input files/context to embed (inline for <50KB, `--file` args for larger)\n   - Required output sections and frontmatter fields\n   - Machine-readable markers: `EXIT_RECOMMENDATION: CONTINUE|HALT`\n   - Any structural requirements the gate will check\n\n   If prompts collectively exceed ~300 lines, put them in a separate `portify-prompts.md`.\n\n4. **Design gates** — For each output artifact, define:\n   - `GateCriteria` with tier, required frontmatter, min lines, semantic checks\n   - `GateMode` (BLOCKING or TRAILING)\n   - All semantic check functions returning `tuple[bool, str]`\n\n5. **Implement pure-programmatic steps** — Write actual runnable Python code for steps classified as \"pure programmatic\". These run as direct function calls in the executor, bypassing `ClaudeProcess`. Include: file discovery, domain classification, batch assignment, inter-pass filtering, config construction.\n\n6. **Design the executor** — Sprint-style synchronous supervisor:\n   - `ThreadPoolExecutor` for batch parallelism (NOT async/await)\n   - `time.sleep()` polling loops for monitoring\n   - Per-step/batch monitoring with stall detection\n   - `TurnLedger` budget guards before each launch\n   - Runner-authored truth: reports from observed data, not Claude self-reporting\n   - Subprocess isolation (4-layer model) for child Claude sessions\n   - Context injection: prior results compressed into subsequent prompts\n   - Signal-aware shutdown with `SignalHandler`\n\n7. **Plan integration** — Click command group, main.py import, file generation order.\n\n**Output**: `portify-spec.md` (+ optional `portify-prompts.md`) — Complete code spec with models, gates, executor design, pure-programmatic implementations, and integration plan.\n\n**Present to user for approval before Phase 3.**\n\n### Phase 3: Release Spec Synthesis\n\n**Phase 2→3 Entry Gate**: Before beginning Phase 3, verify ALL of the following:\n- Phase 2 contract `status: completed`\n- All blocking checks passed (no unresolved BLOCKING gate failures)\n- Phase 2 `step_mapping` contains ≥1 entry\n\n**STOP** if any entry gate condition fails. Report which condition failed and emit the return contract with `failure_phase: 3, failure_type: prerequisite_failed`.\n\n**Goal**: Generate a complete, reviewed release specification from Phase 1 and Phase 2 outputs. Record the wall clock start time for `phase_3_seconds` timing instrumentation.\n\n**Timing**: Record `phase_3_start = current_time()` at the beginning of this phase. NFR-001 advisory target: Phase 3 should complete within 10 minutes wall clock (non-blocking; exceeding this target emits a warning but does not halt the pipeline).\n\n#### Step 3a: Template Instantiation\n\n1. Load the release spec template from `src/superclaude/examples/release-spec-template.md`\n2. Create a working copy at `{work_dir}/portify-release-spec.md`\n3. Verify the working copy was created successfully and contains the template content\n\n#### Step 3b: Content Population\n\nFill template sections from Phase 1 (workflow analysis) and Phase 2 (pipeline specification) outputs using the following mapping table. For each template section, replace `{{SC_PLACEHOLDER:*}}` sentinels with content derived from the specified source:\n\n| # | Template Section | Source |\n|---|-----------------|--------|\n| 1 | Problem Statement | Derive from source workflow's purpose + why portification is needed |\n| 2 | Solution Overview | Phase 2 pipeline architecture (step graph, executor design) |\n| 2.2 | Workflow / Data Flow | Phase 1 data flow diagram, adapted for the target pipeline |\n| 3 | Functional Requirements | One FR per generated pipeline step from Phase 2 `step_mapping` — every `step_mapping` entry MUST produce a corresponding FR (SC-004) |\n| 4 | Architecture | Phase 2 `module_plan` (new files), Phase 0 prerequisites (modified files) |\n| 4.5 | Data Models | Phase 2 model designs (Config, Status, Result, MonitorState) |\n| 4.6 | Implementation Order | Phase 2 module dependency order |\n| 5.2 | Gate Criteria | Phase 2 `gate_definitions` |\n| 5.3 | Phase Contracts | Phase 1+2 contract schemas |\n| 6 | NFRs | Standard portification NFRs (sync execution, gate signatures, runner-authored truth) |\n| 7 | Risk Assessment | Derived from Phase 1 classification confidence scores + unsupported patterns |\n| 8 | Test Plan | Structural test plan from Phase 2 pattern coverage matrix |\n| 10 | Downstream Inputs | Themes for sc:roadmap, tasks for sc:tasklist |\n\nAfter populating all sections, run SC-003 self-validation: verify zero remaining `{{SC_PLACEHOLDER:*}}` sentinels in the working copy. If any remain, resolve them before proceeding.\n\n#### Step 3c: Automated Brainstorm Pass\n\nApply embedded brainstorm behavioral patterns as a non-interactive automated pass against the draft spec. This is NOT an invocation of the `sc:brainstorm` command (which is interactive/Socratic); instead, cycle through each of three personas to analyze the draft spec for gaps:\n\n**Persona perspectives** (apply each in sequence):\n\n1. **Architect persona**: Analyze for structural gaps — missing dependencies, incomplete module boundaries, scaling concerns, cross-module interaction gaps, missing error handling paths\n2. **Analyzer persona**: Analyze for logical gaps — uncovered edge cases, ambiguous requirements, missing acceptance criteria, inconsistent cross-references, untestable requirements\n3. **Backend persona**: Analyze for implementation gaps — missing data models, incomplete API contracts, undefined error states, missing retry/timeout specifications, resource lifecycle gaps\n\n**Structured output format**: Each finding uses the schema:\n```\n{gap_id, description, severity(high|medium|low), affected_section, persona}\n```\n\nExample:\n```\n{GAP-001, \"No retry policy defined for failed gate checks\", medium, \"5.2 Gate Criteria\", architect}\n```\n\n**Zero-gap handling**: If no gaps are identified across all three personas, produce an explicit summary:\n> \"No gaps identified by architect, analyzer, and backend personas. Spec coverage assessed as complete.\"\n\nSet `gaps_identified: 0` in the return contract. Zero gaps is a valid outcome — it does not block the pipeline.\n\n**Output**: Append a `## Brainstorm Gap Analysis` section (Section 12) to the draft spec containing all findings in the structured format, or the zero-gap summary.\n\n#### Step 3d: Gap Incorporation\n\nReview each brainstorm finding and route it:\n\n- **Actionable findings** (findings that can be directly addressed): Incorporate into the relevant spec body section identified by `affected_section`. Mark the finding as `[INCORPORATED]` in the gap analysis table.\n- **Unresolvable items** (findings that require external input, are out of scope, or cannot be resolved within the spec): Route to Section 11 (Open Items) with the gap ID, question, impact, and resolution target. Mark the finding as `[OPEN]` in the gap analysis table.\n\nAfter incorporation, update the gap analysis summary with counts: `{total_gaps, incorporated, open, severity_distribution}`.\n\n**Timing**: Record `phase_3_end = current_time()`. Compute `phase_3_seconds = phase_3_end - phase_3_start`. Populate `phase_timing.phase_3_seconds` in the return contract. If `phase_3_seconds > 600`, emit warning: \"Phase 3 exceeded 10-minute advisory target (NFR-001)\".\n\n**Output**: `{work_dir}/portify-release-spec.md` — Complete draft spec with brainstorm gap analysis section and incorporated findings.\n\n**Phase 3→4 automatic gate**: Draft spec populated (no `{{SC_PLACEHOLDER:*}}` values remain) AND brainstorm section (Section 12) present in draft spec.\n\n### Phase 4: Spec Panel Review\n\nEmbed `sc:spec-panel` behavioral patterns in a convergent review loop. Like Phase 3's brainstorm, this embeds spec-panel behavioral patterns directly rather than invoking the `sc:spec-panel` command.\n\n**4a. Focus pass**: Apply spec-panel behavioral patterns with `--focus correctness,architecture` against `portify-release-spec.md`. This pass applies Fowler (architecture), Nygard (reliability/failure modes), Whittaker (adversarial), Crispin (testing) expert analysis. Produces guard condition boundary tables, validates pipeline dimensional analysis, and produces state variable registry if applicable.\n\n**4b. Focus incorporation**: Review focus findings. Incorporation MUST be additive-only — extend or append to spec sections, do not rewrite existing content.\n- CRITICAL findings: MUST be addressed — either incorporated into spec or documented with a written justification for dismissal in the panel report\n- MAJOR findings: incorporated into spec body\n- MINOR findings: go to Open Items if not immediately actionable\n\n**4c. Critique pass**: Apply spec-panel behavioral patterns with `--mode critique` against the updated spec. Runs the full expert panel in review sequence.\n\n**4d. Convergence check**: Compare critique findings with focus findings. If ≤3 new CRITICAL or MAJOR findings, the spec has converged. Otherwise, loop back to 4b (max 3 iterations; escalate to user if exceeded).\n\n**Present final spec to user for approval before delivering.**\n\n## Decision Framework: What Becomes Programmatic\n\nThe value of portification is moving orchestration out of inference. Here are concrete examples from tested workflows:\n\n| Operation | Classification | Why |\n|-----------|---------------|-----|\n| Enumerate repo files | Pure programmatic | `git ls-files` + pattern matching is deterministic |\n| Classify file domains | Pure programmatic | Extension/path pattern rules, no judgment needed |\n| Assign files to batches | Pure programmatic | Math: divide files by batch_size, assign to agents |\n| Filter Pass 1 results for Pass 2 | Pure programmatic | Parse markdown, extract classifications, filter list |\n| Analyze file for issues | Claude-assisted | Requires reading code, understanding context |\n| Score variant quality | Hybrid | Formulas are programmatic, rubric evaluation is Claude |\n| Validate structural integrity | Pure programmatic | Regex checks, section presence, field counts |\n| Spot-check verification | Claude-assisted | Re-reads files, re-evaluates claims independently |\n| Merge batch reports | Claude-assisted | Requires synthesis, deduplication, pattern extraction |\n| Compute convergence score | Pure programmatic | `agreed / total` — arithmetic |\n| Generate executive summary | Claude-assisted | Requires narrative synthesis |\n\n### Rule of Thumb\nIf you can write a Python function for it with clear input→output types and no ambiguity, make it programmatic. If it requires reading natural language, making judgments, or synthesizing information, use Claude with a gate to verify the output.\n\n## Pipeline Design Principles\n\nThese inform Phase 2 pipeline specification and align with the unified-audit-gating architecture in `pipeline/`.\n\n### Critical Constraints\n1. **Synchronous execution** — Sprint uses `threading` + `time.sleep()` polling. Use `concurrent.futures.ThreadPoolExecutor` for batch parallelism. Do NOT use async/await.\n2. **Gate function signatures** — All semantic checks return `tuple[bool, str]`. The reason string feeds diagnostics and retry decisions.\n3. **Runner-authored truth** — Reports derive from runner-observed data (exit codes, artifacts, gates, monitor signals), not Claude's self-reported status.\n4. **Deterministic flow control** — Python makes all decisions about what runs next. Claude never decides \"what's next\".\n\n### Shared Pipeline Patterns\n5. **Reuse `pipeline/` primitives** — `PipelineConfig`, `Step`, `StepResult`, `GateMode`, `GateCriteria`, `SemanticCheck`, `gate_passed()`, `ClaudeProcess`\n6. **Gate modes** — `BLOCKING` (default) stops pipeline on failure. `TRAILING` defers evaluation. Use trailing only for quality checks that don't affect downstream data flow.\n7. **Turn budget** — `TurnLedger` with debit/credit/guard for multi-subprocess pipelines. Pre-launch guards prevent launching when budget too low.\n8. **Subprocess isolation** — 4-layer model: scoped work dir, git ceiling, isolated plugin dir, isolated settings dir.\n9. **Context injection** — Prior results serialized into subsequent prompts. Compress older, preserve recent.\n10. **Resume-first failures** — On halt: exact resume command, remaining work, diagnostic path, budget suggestion.\n11. **Diagnostic chain** — Runner-side failure analysis that doesn't consume turn budget.\n\n### Output Guidance\n- `portify-analysis.md`: Under 400 lines. Step graph, gates, data flow.\n- `portify-spec.md`: Split prompts to separate file if spec exceeds 800 lines.\n- Pure-programmatic steps: Full implementation code, not descriptions.\n\n## Boundaries\n\n### Will Do\n- Analyze any SuperClaude skill/command/agent workflow\n- Decompose into structured pipeline specification\n- Generate a complete release specification via template instantiation and brainstorm pass\n- Run spec panel review for quality validation\n- Produce a downstream-ready spec for sc:roadmap and sc:tasklist\n\n### Will Not Do\n- Generate code files directly (use the release spec with sc:implement instead)\n- Execute the generated pipeline\n- Modify original skill/command/agent files\n- Create new skills or agents\n- Make architectural decisions about the workflow's logic\n\n## Related Commands\n\n- `/sc:implement` — General feature implementation\n- `/sc:design` — System architecture design\n- `/sc:analyze` — Code analysis for understanding workflows\n- `/sc:build` — Build and compile after generating\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":6,"oldLines":7,"newStart":6,"newLines":7,"lines":[" allowed-tools: Read, Glob, Grep, Edit, Write, Bash, TodoWrite, Task"," mcp-servers: [sequential, serena, context7, auggie-mcp]"," personas: [architect, analyzer, backend]","-argument-hint: \"--workflow <skill-name-or-path> [--name <cli-name>] [--output <dir>] [--dry-run] [--skip-integration]\"","+argument-hint: \"--workflow <skill-name-or-path> [--name <cli-name>] [--output <dir>] [--dry-run]\""," ---"," "," # sc:cli-portify — Workflow-to-CLI Pipeline Compiler"]}],"userModified":false,"replaceAll":false}}

{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01BrsJ4aTDWiYc4ywvpxN8Wa","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→---\n     2→name: sc-cli-portify-protocol\n     3→description: \"Full behavioral protocol for sc:cli-portify — port inference-based SuperClaude workflows into programmatic CLI pipelines with sprint-style supervised execution.\"\n     4→category: development\n     5→complexity: high\n     6→allowed-tools: Read, Glob, Grep, Edit, Write, Bash, TodoWrite, Task\n     7→mcp-servers: [sequential, serena, context7, auggie-mcp]\n     8→personas: [architect, analyzer, backend]\n     9→argument-hint: \"--workflow <skill-name-or-path> [--name <cli-name>] [--output <dir>] [--dry-run]\"\n    10→---\n    11→\n    12→# sc:cli-portify — Workflow-to-CLI Pipeline Compiler\n    13→\n    14→Convert inference-based SuperClaude workflows into programmatic CLI pipelines that ensure 100% completion and consistency between runs.\n    15→\n    16→## Purpose\n    17→\n    18→SuperClaude workflows implemented as commands + skills + agents + refs rely entirely on Claude's reasoning for orchestration. This works well for flexible, one-off tasks but breaks down for repeatable multi-step pipelines where you need:\n    19→\n    20→- **Deterministic control flow** — Python decides what runs when, not inference\n    21→- **Formal artifact validation** — Gates check output quality programmatically\n    22→- **Resume/retry** — Failed steps resume without re-running everything\n    23→- **Live monitoring** — TUI shows progress, stall detection, diagnostics\n    24→- **Budget economics** — Turn ledger tracks consumption across subprocesses\n    25→- **Consistent behavior** — Same inputs produce structurally identical outputs every run\n    26→\n    27→The existing `pipeline/` and `sprint/` modules already solve these problems. This skill bridges the gap by analyzing a workflow and generating a new CLI module that uses these proven patterns.\n    28→\n    29→## What Gets Generated\n    30→\n    31→A CLI subcommand package under `src/superclaude/cli/<name>/`:\n    32→\n    33→| File | Purpose | When Generated |\n    34→|------|---------|----------------|\n    35→| `models.py` | Domain types extending `PipelineConfig`, `Step`, `StepResult` | Always |\n    36→| `gates.py` | `GateCriteria` + semantic check functions returning `tuple[bool, str]` | Always |\n    37→| `prompts.py` | LLM contract builders per Claude-assisted step | Always |\n    38→| `config.py` | CLI arg resolution, file discovery, config construction | Always |\n    39→| `executor.py` | Synchronous supervisor loop with `ThreadPoolExecutor` for parallelism | Always |\n    40→| `monitor.py` | NDJSON incremental output parser with domain signals | Always |\n    41→| `process.py` | `ClaudeProcess` subclass with domain-specific prompt building | Always |\n    42→| `tui.py` | Rich live dashboard with gate state machine | Always |\n    43→| `logging_.py` | Dual JSONL + Markdown execution logging | Always |\n    44→| `diagnostics.py` | `DiagnosticCollector`, `FailureClassifier`, `ReportGenerator` | Always |\n    45→| `commands.py` | Click CLI group and subcommands | Always |\n    46→| `__init__.py` | Package exports | Always |\n    47→| `inventory.py` | Pure-programmatic file discovery/classification | If workflow has discovery steps |\n    48→| `filtering.py` | Pure-programmatic inter-step data filtering | If workflow has filtering between steps |\n    49→\n    50→These file definitions inform the pipeline specification produced in Phase 2.\n    51→\n    52→## Required Input\n    53→\n    54→```\n    55→/sc:cli-portify --workflow <skill-name-or-path> [--name <cli-name>] [--output <dir>]\n    56→```\n    57→\n    58→| Argument | Required | Description |\n    59→|----------|----------|-------------|\n    60→| `--workflow` | Yes | Skill directory path or `sc-*` name to portify |\n    61→| `--name` | No | CLI subcommand name (default: derived from workflow) |\n    62→| `--output` | No | Output directory (default: `src/superclaude/cli/<name>/`) |\n    63→| `--dry-run` | No | Show decomposition plan without generating spec |\n    64→\n    65→**STOP** if `--workflow` is not provided or the path doesn't resolve to a valid skill.\n    66→\n    67→## Behavioral Flow\n    68→\n    69→Four phases, each producing artifacts that feed the next. Present output to user for review after Phases 1 and 2 before continuing.\n    70→\n    71→### Phase 1: Workflow Analysis\n    72→\n    73→Load `refs/analysis-protocol.md` before this phase. It contains the discovery checklist, step decomposition algorithm, classification rubric, and output format template.\n    74→\n    75→**Goal**: Decompose the target workflow into a structured pipeline specification.\n    76→\n    77→1. **Discover components** — Find the command `.md`, skill `SKILL.md`, all `refs/` and `rules/`, all `templates/`, all `scripts/`, and all referenced agents. Build a component inventory table with paths, line counts, and purposes.\n    78→\n    79→2. **Map the protocol** — Extract the step-by-step behavioral flow. Pay attention to:\n    80→   - Wave/phase boundaries in the skill\n    81→   - Agent delegation patterns (which agent, parallel vs sequential)\n    82→   - Conditional execution paths (flags that skip steps)\n    83→   - Implicit inter-step data flow (what one step produces that another consumes)\n    84→\n    85→3. **Identify steps** — A new Step boundary exists when:\n    86→   - A new artifact is produced\n    87→   - A different agent takes over\n    88→   - Execution mode changes (sequential → parallel)\n    89→   - A quality gate must be evaluated\n    90→   - Operation type changes (analysis → generation → validation)\n    91→\n    92→4. **Classify each step** on the programmatic spectrum:\n    93→   - **Pure programmatic**: Runs as a Python function, no Claude subprocess. Examples: file inventory via `git ls-files`, config construction, file filtering between passes, scoring formulas, structural validation, batch assignment. If the logic is deterministic and the input/output formats are well-defined, it should be programmatic.\n    94→   - **Claude-assisted**: Runs as a Claude subprocess with a prompt contract and gate. Examples: content analysis, writing reports, rubric-based assessment, creative synthesis, debate.\n    95→   - **Hybrid**: Programmatic setup → Claude subprocess → programmatic validation. Examples: steps that need Claude for content but have strict structural validation on the output.\n    96→\n    97→5. **Map dependencies and parallel groups** — Draw the data flow: which steps produce artifacts consumed by downstream steps? Which steps are independent and can run concurrently? For batched workflows, identify where batch parallelism applies.\n    98→\n    99→6. **Extract gates** — For each step output, identify what validation the original workflow expects. Map these to gate tiers: EXEMPT (informational), LIGHT (exists + non-empty), STANDARD (structural checks), STRICT (structural + semantic).\n   100→\n   101→7. **Assign gate modes** — `GateMode.BLOCKING` for steps whose output feeds downstream steps. `GateMode.TRAILING` for quality-only checks that don't affect data flow.\n   102→\n   103→**Output**: `portify-analysis.md` — Complete decomposition following the template in `refs/analysis-protocol.md`. Must include: component inventory, step graph with classifications, parallel groups, gates summary, data flow diagram, and recommendations.\n   104→\n   105→**Present to user for review before Phase 2.**\n   106→\n   107→### Phase 2: Pipeline Specification\n   108→\n   109→Load `refs/pipeline-spec.md` before this phase. It contains Step definition patterns, model design patterns, gate patterns, executor patterns, and the new unified-audit-gating patterns (TurnLedger, gate modes, subprocess isolation, context injection, resume semantics).\n   110→\n   111→**Goal**: Convert the analysis into concrete, code-ready specifications.\n   112→\n   113→1. **Design the Step graph** — Map each workflow step to `Step` objects. Batched parallel steps are `list[Step]` groups. Dynamic step counts (e.g., batch count determined at runtime) require a `build_steps()` function.\n   114→\n   115→2. **Define models** — Design domain-specific dataclasses:\n   116→   - Config extending `PipelineConfig` with workflow-specific fields (source paths, pass selection, batch sizes, stall/timeout policies)\n   117→   - Status enum with domain-specific states (e.g., `VALIDATION_FAIL`, `CRITICAL_FAIL` for audit workflows)\n   118→   - Result extending `StepResult` with execution telemetry\n   119→   - Aggregate result with `resume_command()` and `suggested_resume_budget`\n   120→   - Monitor state with domain-specific NDJSON signals\n   121→   - `TurnLedger` integration for budget tracking\n   122→\n   123→3. **Design prompts** — For each Claude-assisted step, write the prompt builder. Each prompt must specify:\n   124→   - What input files/context to embed (inline for <50KB, `--file` args for larger)\n   125→   - Required output sections and frontmatter fields\n   126→   - Machine-readable markers: `EXIT_RECOMMENDATION: CONTINUE|HALT`\n   127→   - Any structural requirements the gate will check\n   128→\n   129→   If prompts collectively exceed ~300 lines, put them in a separate `portify-prompts.md`.\n   130→\n   131→4. **Design gates** — For each output artifact, define:\n   132→   - `GateCriteria` with tier, required frontmatter, min lines, semantic checks\n   133→   - `GateMode` (BLOCKING or TRAILING)\n   134→   - All semantic check functions returning `tuple[bool, str]`\n   135→\n   136→5. **Implement pure-programmatic steps** — Write actual runnable Python code for steps classified as \"pure programmatic\". These run as direct function calls in the executor, bypassing `ClaudeProcess`. Include: file discovery, domain classification, batch assignment, inter-pass filtering, config construction.\n   137→\n   138→6. **Design the executor** — Sprint-style synchronous supervisor:\n   139→   - `ThreadPoolExecutor` for batch parallelism (NOT async/await)\n   140→   - `time.sleep()` polling loops for monitoring\n   141→   - Per-step/batch monitoring with stall detection\n   142→   - `TurnLedger` budget guards before each launch\n   143→   - Runner-authored truth: reports from observed data, not Claude self-reporting\n   144→   - Subprocess isolation (4-layer model) for child Claude sessions\n   145→   - Context injection: prior results compressed into subsequent prompts\n   146→   - Signal-aware shutdown with `SignalHandler`\n   147→\n   148→7. **Plan integration** — Click command group, main.py import, file generation order.\n   149→\n   150→**Output**: `portify-spec.md` (+ optional `portify-prompts.md`) — Complete code spec with models, gates, executor design, pure-programmatic implementations, and integration plan.\n   151→\n   152→**Present to user for approval before Phase 3.**\n   153→\n   154→### Phase 3: Release Spec Synthesis\n   155→\n   156→**Phase 2→3 Entry Gate**: Before beginning Phase 3, verify ALL of the following:\n   157→- Phase 2 contract `status: completed`\n   158→- All blocking checks passed (no unresolved BLOCKING gate failures)\n   159→- Phase 2 `step_mapping` contains ≥1 entry\n   160→\n   161→**STOP** if any entry gate condition fails. Report which condition failed and emit the return contract with `failure_phase: 3, failure_type: prerequisite_failed`.\n   162→\n   163→**Goal**: Generate a complete, reviewed release specification from Phase 1 and Phase 2 outputs. Record the wall clock start time for `phase_3_seconds` timing instrumentation.\n   164→\n   165→**Timing**: Record `phase_3_start = current_time()` at the beginning of this phase. NFR-001 advisory target: Phase 3 should complete within 10 minutes wall clock (non-blocking; exceeding this target emits a warning but does not halt the pipeline).\n   166→\n   167→#### Step 3a: Template Instantiation\n   168→\n   169→1. Load the release spec template from `src/superclaude/examples/release-spec-template.md`\n   170→2. Create a working copy at `{work_dir}/portify-release-spec.md`\n   171→3. Verify the working copy was created successfully and contains the template content\n   172→\n   173→#### Step 3b: Content Population\n   174→\n   175→Fill template sections from Phase 1 (workflow analysis) and Phase 2 (pipeline specification) outputs using the following mapping table. For each template section, replace `{{SC_PLACEHOLDER:*}}` sentinels with content derived from the specified source:\n   176→\n   177→| # | Template Section | Source |\n   178→|---|-----------------|--------|\n   179→| 1 | Problem Statement | Derive from source workflow's purpose + why portification is needed |\n   180→| 2 | Solution Overview | Phase 2 pipeline architecture (step graph, executor design) |\n   181→| 2.2 | Workflow / Data Flow | Phase 1 data flow diagram, adapted for the target pipeline |\n   182→| 3 | Functional Requirements | One FR per generated pipeline step from Phase 2 `step_mapping` — every `step_mapping` entry MUST produce a corresponding FR (SC-004) |\n   183→| 4 | Architecture | Phase 2 `module_plan` (new files), Phase 0 prerequisites (modified files) |\n   184→| 4.5 | Data Models | Phase 2 model designs (Config, Status, Result, MonitorState) |\n   185→| 4.6 | Implementation Order | Phase 2 module dependency order |\n   186→| 5.2 | Gate Criteria | Phase 2 `gate_definitions` |\n   187→| 5.3 | Phase Contracts | Phase 1+2 contract schemas |\n   188→| 6 | NFRs | Standard portification NFRs (sync execution, gate signatures, runner-authored truth) |\n   189→| 7 | Risk Assessment | Derived from Phase 1 classification confidence scores + unsupported patterns |\n   190→| 8 | Test Plan | Structural test plan from Phase 2 pattern coverage matrix |\n   191→| 10 | Downstream Inputs | Themes for sc:roadmap, tasks for sc:tasklist |\n   192→\n   193→After populating all sections, run SC-003 self-validation: verify zero remaining `{{SC_PLACEHOLDER:*}}` sentinels in the working copy. If any remain, resolve them before proceeding.\n   194→\n   195→#### Step 3c: Automated Brainstorm Pass\n   196→\n   197→Apply embedded brainstorm behavioral patterns as a non-interactive automated pass against the draft spec. This is NOT an invocation of the `sc:brainstorm` command (which is interactive/Socratic); instead, cycle through each of three personas to analyze the draft spec for gaps:\n   198→\n   199→**Persona perspectives** (apply each in sequence):\n   200→\n   201→1. **Architect persona**: Analyze for structural gaps — missing dependencies, incomplete module boundaries, scaling concerns, cross-module interaction gaps, missing error handling paths\n   202→2. **Analyzer persona**: Analyze for logical gaps — uncovered edge cases, ambiguous requirements, missing acceptance criteria, inconsistent cross-references, untestable requirements\n   203→3. **Backend persona**: Analyze for implementation gaps — missing data models, incomplete API contracts, undefined error states, missing retry/timeout specifications, resource lifecycle gaps\n   204→\n   205→**Structured output format**: Each finding uses the schema:\n   206→```\n   207→{gap_id, description, severity(high|medium|low), affected_section, persona}\n   208→```\n   209→\n   210→Example:\n   211→```\n   212→{GAP-001, \"No retry policy defined for failed gate checks\", medium, \"5.2 Gate Criteria\", architect}\n   213→```\n   214→\n   215→**Zero-gap handling**: If no gaps are identified across all three personas, produce an explicit summary:\n   216→> \"No gaps identified by architect, analyzer, and backend personas. Spec coverage assessed as complete.\"\n   217→\n   218→Set `gaps_identified: 0` in the return contract. Zero gaps is a valid outcome — it does not block the pipeline.\n   219→\n   220→**Output**: Append a `## Brainstorm Gap Analysis` section (Section 12) to the draft spec containing all findings in the structured format, or the zero-gap summary.\n   221→\n   222→#### Step 3d: Gap Incorporation\n   223→\n   224→Review each brainstorm finding and route it:\n   225→\n   226→- **Actionable findings** (findings that can be directly addressed): Incorporate into the relevant spec body section identified by `affected_section`. Mark the finding as `[INCORPORATED]` in the gap analysis table.\n   227→- **Unresolvable items** (findings that require external input, are out of scope, or cannot be resolved within the spec): Route to Section 11 (Open Items) with the gap ID, question, impact, and resolution target. Mark the finding as `[OPEN]` in the gap analysis table.\n   228→\n   229→After incorporation, update the gap analysis summary with counts: `{total_gaps, incorporated, open, severity_distribution}`.\n   230→\n   231→**Timing**: Record `phase_3_end = current_time()`. Compute `phase_3_seconds = phase_3_end - phase_3_start`. Populate `phase_timing.phase_3_seconds` in the return contract. If `phase_3_seconds > 600`, emit warning: \"Phase 3 exceeded 10-minute advisory target (NFR-001)\".\n   232→\n   233→**Output**: `{work_dir}/portify-release-spec.md` — Complete draft spec with brainstorm gap analysis section and incorporated findings.\n   234→\n   235→**Phase 3→4 automatic gate**: Draft spec populated (no `{{SC_PLACEHOLDER:*}}` values remain) AND brainstorm section (Section 12) present in draft spec.\n   236→\n   237→### Phase 4: Spec Panel Review\n   238→\n   239→Embed `sc:spec-panel` behavioral patterns in a convergent review loop. Like Phase 3's brainstorm, this embeds spec-panel behavioral patterns directly rather than invoking the `sc:spec-panel` command.\n   240→\n   241→**4a. Focus pass**: Apply spec-panel behavioral patterns with `--focus correctness,architecture` against `portify-release-spec.md`. This pass applies Fowler (architecture), Nygard (reliability/failure modes), Whittaker (adversarial), Crispin (testing) expert analysis. Produces guard condition boundary tables, validates pipeline dimensional analysis, and produces state variable registry if applicable.\n   242→\n   243→**4b. Focus incorporation**: Review focus findings. Incorporation MUST be additive-only — extend or append to spec sections, do not rewrite existing content.\n   244→- CRITICAL findings: MUST be addressed — either incorporated into spec or documented with a written justification for dismissal in the panel report\n   245→- MAJOR findings: incorporated into spec body\n   246→- MINOR findings: go to Open Items if not immediately actionable\n   247→\n   248→**4c. Critique pass**: Apply spec-panel behavioral patterns with `--mode critique` against the updated spec. Runs the full expert panel in review sequence.\n   249→\n   250→**4d. Convergence check**: Compare critique findings with focus findings. If ≤3 new CRITICAL or MAJOR findings, the spec has converged. Otherwise, loop back to 4b (max 3 iterations; escalate to user if exceeded).\n   251→\n   252→**Present final spec to user for approval before delivering.**\n   253→\n   254→## Decision Framework: What Becomes Programmatic\n   255→\n   256→The value of portification is moving orchestration out of inference. Here are concrete examples from tested workflows:\n   257→\n   258→| Operation | Classification | Why |\n   259→|-----------|---------------|-----|\n   260→| Enumerate repo files | Pure programmatic | `git ls-files` + pattern matching is deterministic |\n   261→| Classify file domains | Pure programmatic | Extension/path pattern rules, no judgment needed |\n   262→| Assign files to batches | Pure programmatic | Math: divide files by batch_size, assign to agents |\n   263→| Filter Pass 1 results for Pass 2 | Pure programmatic | Parse markdown, extract classifications, filter list |\n   264→| Analyze file for issues | Claude-assisted | Requires reading code, understanding context |\n   265→| Score variant quality | Hybrid | Formulas are programmatic, rubric evaluation is Claude |\n   266→| Validate structural integrity | Pure programmatic | Regex checks, section presence, field counts |\n   267→| Spot-check verification | Claude-assisted | Re-reads files, re-evaluates claims independently |\n   268→| Merge batch reports | Claude-assisted | Requires synthesis, deduplication, pattern extraction |\n   269→| Compute convergence score | Pure programmatic | `agreed / total` — arithmetic |\n   270→| Generate executive summary | Claude-assisted | Requires narrative synthesis |\n   271→\n   272→### Rule of Thumb\n   273→If you can write a Python function for it with clear input→output types and no ambiguity, make it programmatic. If it requires reading natural language, making judgments, or synthesizing information, use Claude with a gate to verify the output.\n   274→\n   275→## Pipeline Design Principles\n   276→\n   277→These inform Phase 2 pipeline specification and align with the unified-audit-gating architecture in `pipeline/`.\n   278→\n   279→### Critical Constraints\n   280→1. **Synchronous execution** — Sprint uses `threading` + `time.sleep()` polling. Use `concurrent.futures.ThreadPoolExecutor` for batch parallelism. Do NOT use async/await.\n   281→2. **Gate function signatures** — All semantic checks return `tuple[bool, str]`. The reason string feeds diagnostics and retry decisions.\n   282→3. **Runner-authored truth** — Reports derive from runner-observed data (exit codes, artifacts, gates, monitor signals), not Claude's self-reported status.\n   283→4. **Deterministic flow control** — Python makes all decisions about what runs next. Claude never decides \"what's next\".\n   284→\n   285→### Shared Pipeline Patterns\n   286→5. **Reuse `pipeline/` primitives** — `PipelineConfig`, `Step`, `StepResult`, `GateMode`, `GateCriteria`, `SemanticCheck`, `gate_passed()`, `ClaudeProcess`\n   287→6. **Gate modes** — `BLOCKING` (default) stops pipeline on failure. `TRAILING` defers evaluation. Use trailing only for quality checks that don't affect downstream data flow.\n   288→7. **Turn budget** — `TurnLedger` with debit/credit/guard for multi-subprocess pipelines. Pre-launch guards prevent launching when budget too low.\n   289→8. **Subprocess isolation** — 4-layer model: scoped work dir, git ceiling, isolated plugin dir, isolated settings dir.\n   290→9. **Context injection** — Prior results serialized into subsequent prompts. Compress older, preserve recent.\n   291→10. **Resume-first failures** — On halt: exact resume command, remaining work, diagnostic path, budget suggestion.\n   292→11. **Diagnostic chain** — Runner-side failure analysis that doesn't consume turn budget.\n   293→\n   294→### Output Guidance\n   295→- `portify-analysis.md`: Under 400 lines. Step graph, gates, data flow.\n   296→- `portify-spec.md`: Split prompts to separate file if spec exceeds 800 lines.\n   297→- Pure-programmatic steps: Full implementation code, not descriptions.\n   298→\n   299→## Boundaries\n   300→\n   301→### Will Do\n   302→- Analyze any SuperClaude skill/command/agent workflow\n   303→- Decompose into structured pipeline specification\n   304→- Generate a complete release specification via template instantiation and brainstorm pass\n   305→- Run spec panel review for quality validation\n   306→- Produce a downstream-ready spec for sc:roadmap and sc:tasklist\n   307→\n   308→### Will Not Do\n   309→- Generate code files directly (use the release spec with sc:implement instead)\n   310→- Execute the generated pipeline\n   311→- Modify original skill/command/agent files\n   312→- Create new skills or agents\n   313→- Make architectural decisions about the workflow's logic\n   314→\n   315→## Related Commands\n   316→\n   317→- `/sc:implement` — General feature implementation\n   318→- `/sc:design` — System architecture design\n   319→- `/sc:analyze` — Code analysis for understanding workflows\n   320→- `/sc:build` — Build and compile after generating\n   321→"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":"toolu_01LPjkFSxw9xLs9tZ3SG31FP","session_id":"e766f3cb-acef-4e77-816a-28945eb21e7c","uuid":"5fac5711-fb33-4acc-a043-4d89de628020"}
